Letter 179

Dear Sir/Madam, This is to inform you that we have received a letter from the Board of Directors of the Shanghai City Dongting Xishan Jinting Guild Hall stating that they were "astonished" to read the report "Reactions to the Jinting Guild Hall Forcibly Collecting Tips," which is inconsistent with the facts. The Board states that it was ordered to renovate the city rooms of the guild hall and did not sign contracts with the tenants. Therefore, it is not subject to any restrictions. It is now unreasonably accused of forcibly collecting tips and should bear the burden of proof. If the tenants cannot produce the receipt issued by the guild hall to Shan Yunsheng, causing the guild hall to suffer any direct or indirect losses, the tenants should bear the responsibility. We request that your lawyer represent us and request that Shen Bao promptly correct the information in the Letter to the Editor section of your newspaper. We would be very grateful for your help. Sincerely, Lawyer Ye Foukang, July 15th,

To the Esteemed Chief Editor of Shen Bao, Greetings, I am writing to you regarding the news article "Dispute over the Jie Fa Steamer Incident" in the June 25th issue of your newspaper. After reading it, I was greatly surprised. The details of the Jie Fa steamer incident differ from what was reported in your newspaper. The report is completely based on rumors and is inaccurate. It is clear that outsiders are unaware of the truth, leading to misinformation. The Jie Fa steamer ran aground near Sang Island in the Bohai Bay on the afternoon of April 13th. The chart indicated a submerged reef. The next day, the shipowner and an employee of the ship hull insurance company (i.e., the Shanghai Lianbao Company), Mr. Jiang Junzhe, hired the　島丸 from the Manchuria Railway Company to provide assistance. Due to the severe damage to the ship's hull, it was already in a semi-sunken state and in extreme danger. As a result, rescue efforts were abandoned, and only the lives of the 58 crew members were saved and returned to Dalian. At the request of the shipowner, the Datong Branch of the Longkou Agency sent personnel to Sang Island to cooperate with the island's security force in guarding the ship on land. On April 20th, the Lianbao Company again attempted rescue, requesting the shipowner's representative, Cai Lu, to provide assistance. On the same day, they hired the Song丸 from the Songpu Steamship Company together with Jiang Junzhe, and it was agreed to set sail from Dalian on the 22nd. For the sake of time and economy, the shipowner's representative, Cai Lu, was instructed to first take the Song丸 to the Datong Branch of the Longkou Agency to arrange for the necessary tugboats, sampans, and coolie tools for the rescue, so that the Song丸 could immediately take the tugboats and coolies to the rescue upon arrival in Longkou. On April 20th, Jiang Junzhe of the Lianbao Company, along with several others, sailed from Dalian on the Song丸. On the morning of the 23rd, they arrived at the site of the Jie Fa incident. Jiang Junzhe and others personally boarded the Jie Fa to inspect it. In the afternoon of the same day, they left the Jie Fa at Sang Island and arrived in Longkou around 4 PM. They had a cordial conversation with the shipowner's representative and the manager of the Datong Branch, stating that the hull and remaining cargo of the Jie Fa were in the same condition as when it ran aground, without any movement. They also praised the guards for their diligent watch. On the same day, due to the late hour, only the hired coolies and tools were sent to the Song丸, preparing to go to the rescue the next morning. Unexpectedly, on the 24th, a strong wind and rough waves prevented the tugboats from working and the Song丸 from proceeding. It was reluctantly postponed until 6:30 AM on the 25th, when Jiang Junzhe, along with several others, as well as Cai Lutong, the manager of the Datong Company, boarded the Song丸 for the rescue. On the way, they discovered the Jie Fa was on fire. By the time they arrived at the scene, the fire was too intense to approach. The Sang Island security force sent personnel to report to the Song丸. They said that the fire in the stern of the Jie Fa was discovered around midnight on the 24th. Although the cause of the fire was unknown, the land and sea of Sang Island were exceptionally peaceful, and there had never been any incidents of robbers or pirates. Furthermore, there were no ships approaching the Jie Fa before or after the fire. These are the facts of the incident. As the ship had been destroyed, there was no need for the guards to continue watching. They were all withdrawn to Longkou on the same day. The report in your newspaper that the shipowner sent six tugboats from Longkou and guards to the wrecked ship to salvage cargo, resulting in the death of Feng Lianrong and the payment of condolences, is completely false. As for the alleged control of the Lee Township head of San Island in Huang County, it is a riot due to infighting on the island, and is unrelated to the Jie Fa incident. I have provided a detailed account of the facts in order to clarify the truth and avoid misunderstandings. Shipowner Representative Cai Lu Proxy Longkou Datong Branch

Incoming Piece 180

Principles and Standards for Abolishing the Tael and Adopting the Yuan (Continued) by Xu Peikun 181

(C) The Origin of Monetary Disputes. The disputes arising from the coexistence of taels and yuans, as explained previously, are not as serious as commonly perceived. Therefore, using this point as the rationale for currency reform is inadequate. However, whether China's monetary disputes are limited to the relationship between taels and yuans or if other monetary disputes exist should be noted and analyzed by us. In my observation, the disputes between taels and yuans are relatively minor. The significant monetary disputes in China lie in the differences in silver scales across regions, the variations in various silver dollars, the inconsistencies in various small silver coins, and other subsidiary currencies, as well as the differences in various paper currencies across regions. These numerous disputes concerning hard and light currencies are well understood by both the silver and money circles. If they are not resolved and only the conversion from taels to yuans is addressed, today's plan to abolish the tael and adopt the yuan will be nothing more than a pipe dream. Lastly, international settlement involves many disputes in gold and silver conversions. The procedures for converting various silver dollars into various silver taels and then into various gold dollars are numerous, and the discrepancies are significant. The rise and fall of foreign exchange rates, even by a fraction of a cent, can result in substantial gains or losses beyond description. If the foreign exchange rate is fixed at 7.2 mace, the conversion calculation will be much more convenient, and extraneous gains or losses can be avoided. It is hoped that after the foreign exchange rate is fixed, a portion of the conversion disputes in gold and silver settlements can be resolved. However, many disputes still arise from the fluctuation of silver prices and the changing ratios between gold and silver. Today, we are vociferously advocating for the abolition of the tael and the adoption of the yuan, but whether this dispute can be resolved and whether it will be practically beneficial are preliminary issues. As things stand, the gold-silver ratio may not be a problem, and abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan is indeed a good remedy for the problem. Previous advocates for a gold standard mostly based their arguments on the changing gold-silver ratio. However, the unsuitability of the gold standard for our national conditions has been conclusively proven by the facts of the past year and cannot be denied. Moreover, most countries have abandoned the gold standard, with only one or two countries struggling to maintain it, only to fail in the end. In the future, various countries may adopt a bimetallic standard or a special standard, which is currently being brewing. However, in any case, various countries will certainly add silver coins and carefully plan ways to stabilize the gold-silver ratio. Therefore, after China abolishes the tael and adopts the yuan, disputes in gold and silver settlements are expected to gradually decrease, and I firmly believe that China will be a beneficiary.

(D) Principles for Abolishing the Tael and Adopting the Yuan. Having understood the above points, we can begin to discuss the principles for abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan. If we want to abolish the tael and adopt the yuan, in addition to resolving the disputes between taels and yuans, we must also resolve the various monetary disputes mentioned above. This is part of the principle. However, the more profound meaning of currency reform lies in seeking to establish a stable and unified national currency system, so that national currency and prices do not fluctuate drastically. It is necessary to ensure that China's currency is indeed a perfect standard for measuring prices, and further, that China's currency can accurately represent the purchasing power of each individual. Furthermore, it should ensure that China's currency is a standard for both material and labor value, and that it can reliably represent the permanent wealth of groups or individuals. It should also ensure that China's currency is a standard that is easy to exchange and suitable for the standard of living. As mentioned above, only the silver yuan unit and a perfect subsidiary currency system can competently fulfill these requirements. Due to space limitations, this article cannot analyze each point in detail. However, generally speaking, the monetary units of various countries in the world are only gold, silver, and paper. The inapplicability of the gold standard to various countries in the world, and even more so to our country, has been discussed in detail over the past year. As for paper currency, it can only be hoped to circulate when the credit system is developed to the extreme. There is no possibility of adopting a paper standard within the next fifty or sixty years. Therefore, China only has the option of adopting the silver yuan unit system. Furthermore, by considering the situation, studying the reasons, and taking both into account, China's decisive adoption of the silver yuan unit system at this time is indeed an excellent opportunity to obtain a perfect monetary system. It is not clear whether those who currently advocate for the abolition of the tael and the adoption of the yuan are advocating for the adoption of a silver standard or are merely using it to resolve local disputes between business taels and yuans. If the latter is the sole intention, it will not only fail to resolve monetary disputes but will also increase them. Treating the headache when the head aches and the foot when the foot aches is the usual trick of incompetent doctors to kill people. This is such a major issue, and it is hoped that the ruling officials will take it seriously and not imitate the actions of incompetent doctors and apply them to the people whose livelihoods are full of wounds. Having decided on the overall principles for abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan as before, implementing reform policies based on these principles will achieve the practical effects of abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan. Otherwise, it will only cause disputes and be of no benefit. (To be continued)

A Skillful Talk

Textual Research on the Soft Language of Wu: Dou, Qie, Zhou 182

— Zhan Lu

The soft language of Wu has never had a specialized book, and there are many well-known sayings that everyone is said to be able to speak. What is written is that everyone cannot write. Why can't they write? It's just because of the changes in sounds. Errors are passed on, resulting in the loss of the true meaning.

I really want to organize the Wu dialect a bit. Although there is a partial rudimentary framework, it is still far from success. I'll first bring up three words that are often said in the mouths of Wu people: (1) The first word cannot be written, so I have to write a fanqie, which is the word "De Ai." In the mouths of Suzhou people, to describe someone as very flattering, they call him "De Ai."

(2) The second word is written incorrectly. Ordinary Suzhou vernacular letters often write the word "Qiu." If the body is not well, it is called "body Qiu." If the goods are not good, it is called "goods Qiu." A person with a bad temper is called "Qiu person."

(3) The third word is also written casually, often written as the word "Zhou." The word "Zhou" and the word "Qiu" have similar meanings, but there is also a distinction: the word "Qiu" represents not strong, and the word "Zhou" represents not straight.

According to my humble opinion, the above three words are not difficult to write. Tracing back to the source, they are probably these three words:

(1) The word "De Ai" was originally the word "Dou." Whenever saying a few flattering words, the more the voice trembles, the more it pleases people; to please people, the Wu dialect calls it the word "Dou." Upon hearing a trembling, intimate voice, they say: Dou de lai—Dou de lai! This word "Dou" was originally a direct cut, but later, through errors, it was read as "Ai Qie," and then as "De Ai Qie"; the words "De" and "Ai" are alliterative; therefore, this word "Dou" is called the combined sound of the two words "De Ai."

(2) The word "Qiu" should be written as the word "Qie"; if the physique is not strong, it is called "body Qie"; if the will is not strong, it is called "temper Qie." Qie is "Qu Jie Qie," Qiu is "Qu Jiu Qie," Qie and Qiu are alliterative. The vulgar errors are all due to the alliteration relationship; therefore, this word "Qie" is also called the word "Qiu."

(3) The word "Zhou" should be written as the word "Zou"; Zou means uneven. Uneven skin is called "Zou skin"; an uneven temper is called "Zou temper." Zou is definitely an oblique tone, and the word "Zhou" is a level tone; the four tones in the mouths of Suzhou people are originally casual; it is no wonder that the oblique tone word "Zou" is read as the level tone word "Zhou."

Preface to Chen Shuren's Collection of Paintings 183

— Wang Jingwei

Mr. Shuren asked me to write a preface to his collection of paintings. I have worked with Mr. Shuren for a long time. During breaks from official duties, we would sometimes discuss poetry, and I often had the opportunity to view Mr. Shuren's paintings. I do not understand painting, and my understanding of poetry is also very shallow. I once wrote in the preface to my own collection of poems:

The Book of Poetry says, "The people are weary, let them have a little rest." How apt are these words. People cannot but labor, and labor cannot be without rest. To labor long and rest briefly is what people should do and also the greatest joy in life. My poems are thus composed at such times. Therefore, my poems cannot be like the images on the cauldrons of Yu, which expose evil, or the warm rhinoceros horn, which illuminates monsters, exhaustively capturing the essence of all things and leaving nothing hidden. They are merely like woodcutters and peddlers, walking a long road under the scorching sun, occasionally laying down their burdens and resting under a tree, sitting together in a circle, singing and laughing, to forget their suffering for a moment. Therefore, I named my collection "A Little Rest."

My understanding of poetry, after more than twenty years of study, is still so shallow. How much more so when it comes to painting, which I have never understood. How can I write a preface for Mr. Shuren? However, Mr. Shuren and I are both committed to the revolution, taking labor and hardship as our lives and sacrifice as our ultimate goal. We do not do it for any pleasure, but because our conscience dictates that we must. The comfort we receive also comes from the joy of a clear conscience. To take too much pleasure in worldly enjoyment is not only damaging to our integrity but will also lead us into sin. Not to mention material desires, even the so-called natural beauty seems impartial to people. However, under dilapidated huts and inside coal mine tunnels, the notion of impartial sunshine and wind naturally has its limitations. Since we cannot be without labor and labor cannot be without rest, then what we take for comfort during these brief rests is that natural beauty is relatively guilt-free. The phenomena of heaven, earth, and all things are noble yet accessible, profound yet candid, pure yet full of change, and they are in seamless harmony with our innocent conscience. Fan Zhongyan said, "Not to be pleased by external gains." At such moments, we no longer know whether we are things or things are us. Between heaven, earth, and all things, there is compassion and no resentment, there is goodness and no evil. We frolic freely, and deceit does not arise. This moment of comfort is more than enough to forget a hundred years of labor and hardship. When emotions stir within us, they are expressed in songs and manifested in paintings. This happens naturally because we do not want this fleeting moment to pass away but seek to prolong and yearn for it endlessly. I ask Mr. Shuren, what do you think?

Northeast Education 185

— Ms. Ye Hua

Mr. Ge Gongzhen recently returned from the Southeast and spoke about the education in the Northeast with extreme pain. The following is a summary. Mr. Ge said that Buddhism considers knowledge as a demon. That is true. The intellectual class in the Northeast, especially in the education sector, is the most miserable. It is impossible to express the pain. If there is indeed a hell in the world, then the Northeast is the hell on earth. And those in the education sector are in the lowest level of hell. They live in a state of not being able to die and not being able to live. There is no way up to heaven and no door down to earth. The mental stimuli they receive often drive people to madness. College students either join the volunteer army or flee for their lives. The innocent are slaughtered one after another. It is confirmed that Fengyong University has been changed to Manchuria University. It will be implemented soon. Secondary schools are currently closed, as they fear that students gathering together will easily incite unrest. A vocational high school outside Shenyang City once prepared to reopen. However, the day before the reopening, each room in the school was plastered with slogans such as "Down with Japan" and "Rather be a Chinese ghost than a puppet slave of a foreign country." When the teachers saw this situation, they gently advised the students to be patient and not to ruin the big plan with small impatience. The reopening and resumption of classes were thus interrupted. Due to the limited time, the textbooks for secondary schools could not be rewritten, so the old textbooks were revised. Whenever the words "Republic of China" appeared, they were all changed to Manchuria. Naturally, any text unfavorable to Japan was deleted. Most of the primary schools have reopened. Primary school students are young and have limited knowledge, so they have no ability to resist Japan. Therefore, Japan takes advantage of their malleability and carefully molds them. The curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education have been completely overturned. Of all the subjects, only five remain: Chinese, Ethics, History, Geography, and Mathematics. All textbooks have been rewritten, focusing on building Manchuria and resisting China. Although the teachers are Chinese, Japanese people often come to the school to supervise and interfere. The teachers, with various grievances, teach with tears in their eyes. Recently, there has been a "Manchuria Founding Movement," forcing primary school students to participate, singing the Manchuria national anthem, and saluting the crossed Manchuria and Japanese flags. The families of primary school students who disobey are often ravaged. Today, education in the Northeast is managed by the Ministry of Education, headed by Zheng Xiaoxu, who follows Japanese instructions. Currently, the Japanese are hiring Japanese education officials who have experience in running schools in Korea to go to the Northeast to take charge of education and culture. They plan to apply the methods of Korea to the Northeast. Alas, who is doing this? Who caused this? How did it come to this?

Record of a Talking Myna Bird 186

— Zhen Yue

Yesterday afternoon, two guests came from Jinshan. One was surnamed Xu, from Fengxian, and the other was surnamed Pan, from Zhujing. They came specifically to visit the Hefeng Agricultural and Forestry Farm. Mr. Xu carried a birdcage with a myna bird inside. As soon as they entered the gate, they hung the cage on the grape trellis. After a while, the myna bird suddenly made sounds like a magpie and a chicken. Then, it spoke in human language, saying, "Myna, myna, myna eats meat." The voice was like that of a child, clear and pleasing to the ear. Mr. Xu said that the bird had been raised for three years and could say many things. It could even shout anti-Japanese slogans. After a moment, the myna bird indeed wagged its small tongue and spoke clearly in human language, saying, "Down with Japan! Down with Japan!" It shouted and jumped as if in great pain and also with a brave posture. It was truly commendable. It is not strange that a myna bird can speak, but it is rare to hear it shout anti-Japanese slogans.

Sandalwood Cannon 187

— Qian Taisheng

The new national hero General Ma Zhanshan raised the banner of righteousness in the Battle of Nenjiang. Recently, he launched a major offensive against the puppet state outside the passes, causing countless brave men of iron and blood to rise up. However, the people inside the passes are no longer as enthusiastically supporting the war as before. This is something that makes people feel deeply saddened.

During the January 28th Incident, the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army and the Volunteer Army fought bravely. The blood of the nation earned international sympathy. The suffering endured by the people in the war zone gave foreigners an even greater stimulus. At that time, whatever the army needed, it was almost granted with a thousand promises. The provinces in the interior reported through radio, rushing to transport day and night. The spirit of cooperation between the army and the people was fully demonstrated in this regard.

We also remember the spirit of joy and excitement of the people when the revolutionary army first arrived in the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang in the 16th year of the Republic of China. The expression of cooperation between the army and the people was definitely not worse than it is now. For example, in the Yanzhou Zhuji area, farmers in the mountains helped the revolutionary army attack Meng Zhaoyue's troops with earthen cannons, reminding people of the people's ardent hopes for the revolutionary army at that time.

This kind of earthen cannon is called a sandalwood cannon. It is made of a kind of hard sandalwood from the mountains. The heart of the tree is carved out, leaving a shell. The outside is wrapped in iron. The cannonballs are also made by local methods, using gunpowder and the hobnails of the villagers' shoes. They can be fired for about three miles with each shot. However, they cannot be used after firing ten shots.

At that time, Meng Zhaoyue's troops said that the revolutionary army's cannonballs had tails. It was truly unimaginable that they were actually the hobnails of the villagers' shoes.

Horse Training Camp Ma Ji 188

— Shou Heng

Mr. Li Jiading, the commander of the Central Army Cavalry Training Corps and the 1st Cavalry Brigade, recently launched a military officer equestrian competition to arouse the interest of learners and promote the attention of the Chinese people. In advance, invitations were sent to various sectors at home and abroad to visit and observe. The following is a review of the grand occasion.

The competition venue was the brigade headquarters' horse field in Xiaoying. Nine types of obstacles were set up, including high bars, double bamboo bars, three-wood bars, wooden walls, and trenches. Everything was available. The highest was about one meter and the widest was about one meter and thirty centimeters. Each obstacle was marked with red, yellow, blue, and white flags. Judges were stationed in various locations. The layout was extremely intricate. Mr. Li reported that due to the limited ability of the horses, there could be no deep equestrian performance. However, what was arranged today was a small angle change of direction and various paces to overcome obstacles. Therefore, it is necessary to have a firm riding position and consistent support between man and horse in order to turn freely and fly over them. On this day, the weather was extremely hot, but the guests were still very enthusiastic. For a time, there was a constant flow of vehicles. Zhu Weizhen of the Military Affairs Commission, Yao Jiecheng, Chen Yi of the Ministry of Military Administration, Zhang Zhizhong, commander of the 5th Army, Foreign Advisor Fo Cai'er, Cavalry Supervisor Wang Haoji, and hundreds of principals, officers, and students of various military specialized schools were present. There were more than 2,000 guests. At about 4 o'clock, the sound of trumpets moved. All the more than 50 participants, led by the brigade chief of staff, arrived in formation. First, a military parade was held, with the brigade commander leading more than 20 representatives of various senior military organs to inspect the horse field. Then, a parade was held before the competition began. In general, the participants were all in high spirits. They soared up and leaped over obstacles, accompanied by melodious and exciting military music, making them even more brave. Applause thundered. The audience cheered wildly. It was truly a sight to behold.

Overseas Talks 189

— Huang Ren

The false eyelashes used by fashionable women in Europe and America are glued to the eyelids with a kind of harmless glue. Black and long ones are considered beautiful. These false eyelashes cost seven shillings and six pence to fifteen shillings per pair and can only be used for two weeks before they need to be replaced with a new pair.

In Victoria, Australia, rats are rampant. They run around day and night and are not afraid of cats. They often attack in groups. At night, people sleep in bed and rats often walk across their bodies.

It is said that playing cards originated in India. Seven hundred years ago, nomadic gypsies went to Europe and brought playing cards with them. From then on, they became popular all over the world and became a common gambling game.

Londoners love flowers. Almost every family uses flowers as decorations. Taking bottled flowers alone, more than 1,200 tons are transported every year. During the flowering season in spring, there are always twenty-five special trains transporting flowers into the city every day.

India has many long forests and abundant grass. Therefore, there are also many snakes. Although doctors have methods to treat snake venom, saving thousands of lives every year, in the past twelve months, more than 25,000 people have died from poisonous snake bites.

American rayon is made entirely from sugarcane residue. Each sugarcane factory must produce 500,000 tons of sugar residue every year for the manufacture of rayon.

There are several specialized doctors in western England. In order to maintain the secrecy of their medicines, they often do not write the names of the drugs on the prescriptions but use numbers instead, ordering patients to go to a designated pharmacy to fill the prescriptions. Only one pharmacist knows what the numbers represent. They have agreed in advance.

The popularity of precious jewelry in England often changes. Last year, rubies, which were ranked fifth, have suddenly become very popular this year. Fashionable women often wear scarlet ornaments, so they have risen from fifth place to first place. Next are beryl, diamonds, pearls, and sapphires.

Casual Notes from Village Life 190

— Xu Muxi

In such hot weather, being able to hide in the countryside and read a little book is considered a blessing by everyone. Therefore, I can get my wish, and I feel that I can force a smile, although since I recognized the human world, the distress of the environment has weighed heavily on me.

This is my hometown. Not long ago, it was forcibly occupied by the enemy, making the virgin who had just come of age even more haggard. Ah! This cold village, this cold village like a deflowered virgin! Secluded dense forests cover the traces of bombing, and the croaking of frogs and the chirping of cicadas interweave to create the symphony of nature; this pain, this annoyance, can never be forgotten.

Although rural life is calm and leisurely, in the madness of the times, the simplicity that shrouded it has also undergone significant changes due to the advancement of the storm. The most sacred and tranquil countryside will henceforth be transformed inland.

The afterglow of the setting sun is a flowing, graceful, gentle sight. Standing by the pond under the willows, chatting with the old farmers in the fields, pursuing life from the pure and honest conversations, in such a clean environment, there is no longer a trace of the atmosphere of urban vices.

The collapse of the rural economy is not a symbol of today. It has long indicated that this is inevitable. However, the farmers are still working hard to remedy the situation, wearing bamboo hats, plowing hard in the fields. The scorching sun has turned their shoulders and backs bronze. This spirit of great fearlessness is the characteristic of the greatest warriors in life, and they have the same value as worship as the soldiers who advance with the sound of drums and horns to eliminate the common enemies of mankind. Warriors, fearless warriors, they are the most worthy of this world, but this world has let them down.

Sugar Market: Raw and White Sugar Showing a Weak but Stable Trend 208

Yesterday, the Sugar Merchant Association's market trading still showed signs of sluggishness, with few transactions. However, the collective sale of No. 24 Dutch raw white sugar by an industry association is gradually taking shape. Market sentiment has slightly improved from stagnation, with transaction prices at 14 taels and 5 cents. The supply is scarce, and the trend remains firm. No. 84 Dutch red sugar is at 10 taels and 7 mace, and raw red sugar is at 12 taels. The market also appears stable. The trading of Taikoo sugar is very sluggish: B mark at 16 taels and 3 mace, CW mark at 15 taels and 8 mace, DY mark at 15 taels and 5.5 mace, and H mark at 12 taels and 5 mace. Although demand is quiet, inventory is low. The company's large volume remains quite firm, so the market situation is relatively stable.

Silk, Tea, Factory Silk Warp Sales Still Not Quiet 209

Yesterday, in the local foreign firm silk market, European and American firms remained inactive. However, silk merchants showed considerable interest in white factory silk warp. Unfortunately, prices tended to be weak. It is estimated that Meiya and other silk factories purchased ten packages of 20-22 thread white factory silk warp for 495 taels. Jinma brand also purchased ten packages of 20-22 thread white factory silk warp for 470 taels. Huangpodun brand purchased ten packages of 13-22 thread white factory silk warp for 490 taels.

No One Inquires About Chang'an Silk Cocoons 210

Native silk factory sales are stagnant... Dry cocoons cannot be mortgaged

Chang'an in Zhejiang has now become the central area of silk production. In recent years, silk fabric sales have plummeted, and both the silk and weaving industries are on the verge of bankruptcy. After the spring cocoons were launched this year, few cocoon businesses opened their scales, and cocoon prices were surprisingly low. Farmers are heavily indebted and generally dry the cocoons themselves. However, the market has become increasingly sluggish, and no one inquires about silk or cocoons. Villagers who still have native silk are affected by the encroachment of artificial silk and Japanese silk. Silk factory sales are stagnant. Those who have dry cocoons and want to mortgage them for cash cannot find anyone to accept them. Farmers' economies are becoming increasingly panicked.

Low-Grade Zhenmei Tea Sells Well, Prices Rise 211

Yesterday, British firms like Yingzhuang Xiehe Yihuo Yulong and others showed strong interest in low-grade Zhenmei green tea from Wenzhou Yushan native estates and other regions. The entire market was very active, and selling prices were 4 or 5 taels higher than before. High-grade Zhenmei teas from Wuyuan Tunxi and other regions had brisk sales of selected teas, while ordinary teas were slightly sluggish. However, inventories of Tunxi, Suian, and Xiuning teas are not abundant, so Chinese tea merchants remain firm in their attitude, and the market is expected to rise without falling.

Coal: Mark and Henan White Coal Market Uniquely Firm and Sought After 212

Recently, the trading of various grades of white coal screenings has been quiet, and selling prices have frequently fallen. However, Mark white coal and Henan white coal are uniquely firm and sought after, refusing to decline easily. Their selling prices exceed those of Hongqi coal. Currently, Mark screenings sell for 19 taels and 5 mace per ton, and Henan screenings sell for 20 taels per ton. The reason is that the available goods are not abundant, and costs are high.

Metals: Large Quantities of Tinplate to be Shipped Back to England 213

The sales of British tinplate in Shanghai are almost surpassing American goods. However, this year's goods are ten times more than in the past, which has caused the market to become weak. It is said that the main reason for this price decline is the impact of the Boxer Indemnity Committee ordering a large quantity of goods (estimated at over 50,000 boxes) from England for shipment to China. Recently, according to reliable sources, the British Chamber of Commerce has telegraphed the Boxer Indemnity Committee to maintain market stability, suggesting that the 28,000+ boxes of goods that have already arrived but not been sold be returned to England. If this happens, the Shanghai market may have hope for recovery.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essays

Studying and Picking Up Girls 214

— Fo

A few days ago, I wrote two articles on "The Truth About Suicide." I still have more to say. I traveled to Suzhou because of some business. Today, I'm changing the topic, but I'll still thoroughly explain the unfinished meaning of the previous articles.

Gentlemen (this "gentlemen" refers to those who pursue love, not ordinary gentlemen), after reading my previous discussions advocating late marriage and discouraging romance, you may be somewhat unhappy and find it unpalatable. It is truly "advising with words that do not please the ear." Today, I will teach you a method for picking up girls. Are you willing to welcome my words?

Do you want to pick up girls? The only condition is to focus on studying. Concentrating on studying and picking up girls are unrelated, so why do I say that it's the only condition? Let me explain. Modern women (this is a common characteristic, not just for women) have a very strong sense of vanity. If you have special talents or excellent knowledge in school, the opposite sex will naturally admire, approach, and look up to you, turning around to "kneel at your feet in your Western suit." Otherwise, no matter how crisp your suit is, how shiny your shoes are, or how much "Stancombe" hair oil you pour on your hair, the opposite sex will absolutely not welcome you. Even if they do, it's "low-class." What do I mean by low-class? Low-level actions that have no meaning. You are probably doing it wrong.

Don't you believe me? In your school, there must be two types of students: those who study hard and have abilities, and those who only like to dress up and act foolish. Ask the "Misses," what is your attitude towards these two types of students? Which type of student do you treat more kindly? You can test it out with this. Look at the important figures with knowledge in the government. Even at an advanced age, there are still several young and beautiful modern "Misses" willing to accommodate them and invite them to fulfill their obligations (this word "obligation" is Chiang Kai-shek's ingenious term). This is very strange.

Furthermore, the concept of marriage will soon be completely eradicated. The Communist Party of Russia has completely abolished the marriage system, transforming it into a "friend-like" spousal system. Even in Eastern and Western countries where the marriage system has not been abolished, many people choose to be free and not marry, waiting until their lives are stable before getting married. So, when you hear that they are getting married, it is very late. As for our country's important figures, they divorce one and marry another, treating married couples as less than friends. Isn't this fundamentally destroying the spousal system? Especially in China, where production is backward, the average commoner finds it difficult to maintain their own livelihood. If they form a family, the burden is even heavier. How can they bear it? The number of suicides is particularly high, perhaps for this reason.

If you completely see through this truth, observe the concept of life with a different perspective, and thoroughly consider the advantages and disadvantages of any undertaking before starting, then it will be appropriate. Otherwise, "blessings can be doors to misfortune." You may be excited now, but you will regret it later!

Literature and Art

Farewell to Sister Yu Renzhi 215

— Ganfang

Spending a few days together in the evening breeze,

Facing the lonely lamp, feeling like a drifting tumbleweed;

The landscape is so difficult to part from,

Especially when I am in sorrow and in a foreign land.

Random Thoughts on Shanghai Changes 216

The east wind in the port of Shanghai is tight,

The sound of the horn is heard everywhere,

The country is only half intact,

Rise and fall depend on the lonely army,

The fire of calamity shines brightly,

The smoke of war connects with the evening clouds,

Who determines the policy of peace?

Officials gather in droves every day.

Hate for the country piles upon each other,

Singing wildly with tears in my eyes,

The sound of the horn is bleak in spring,

The spirit of the people declines daily,

Patriots shed tears for the times,

Generals pledge their hearts to the country,

Forming a river of water,

Rushing forth as a mournful sound.

Science

Silver Engraving Method 217

— Yinglou

Not long ago, I introduced the etching method of copper and iron in this column. This small craft with artistic interest is indeed very valuable. Here, I would like to introduce the silver engraving method. Silver seems to be a softer material compared to other metals. Therefore, sometimes carving with a knife can also be effective. However, the manual method is not as convenient and agile as the chemical method, and it is also more interesting.

The anti-etching agent for silver is generally the same as that for copper and iron. A more convenient method is to mix four parts of beeswax, one part of tallow, five parts of rosin, and ten parts of pine root oil to form a liquid for use.

There are several ways to prepare the etching agent for silver.

(1) Dissolve ten parts of strong nitric acid in twenty parts of water. (If the object to be engraved is larger, add more strong nitric acid and twice the amount of water.) This is a very simple method, and its etching effect is also very strong.

(2) Dissolve thirty grams of potassium chloride in three hundred parts of boiling water. Then dissolve thirty grams of pure hydrochloric acid in three hundred parts of water. Mix the above two solutions together for use. The etching power of this agent is stronger than the first method.

(3) Mix 250 parts of pure nitric acid, 60 parts of ether, 4 parts of acetic acid in 250 parts of water. This agent has a slower chemical reaction and is suitable for fine engraving.

Regarding silver etching engraving, there is a drawback, which is that silver is more expensive. After silver utensils are etched, the scrap silver from the etched parts is completely discarded, which is a pity. However, if you use the first type of etching agent mentioned above, there is a remedy. After strong nitric acid and water etch the silver utensils, there is a kind of silver nitrate left in the liquid. We can add table salt to the liquid. Silver nitrate is combined with the sodium salt of sodium chloride by the缘化反应, precipitating the silver quality and forming white silver chloride. Then filter and dry it. Add the same amount of potassium sodium carbonate as silver chloride, put it in a lead pot, heat it with coal fire, and the original silver quality will be restored, sinking to the bottom of the pot and solidifying into a block. In this way, there is no loss. However, this method is suitable for silver utensils that consume too much silver. If not much is etched away, it is not a pity to discard it, and there is no need to bother.

School Life

Teasing the Teacher 218

— Chen Jingyu

Mr. X, the English teacher at XX School, is good at

dressing up and likes to wear Western suits. Unfortunately, his face is pockmarked, which is his shortcoming. One day, when he was teaching, he had just finished taking attendance, picked up a piece of chalk, and was about to raise his hand to write when he saw a few lines of writing left on the blackboard. He inadvertently read it aloud and was furious: "Nonsense!" "Bullshit!" poured out like a string of beads. Why? Because what was written was:

"Flipped pomegranate skin, mud-printed sole, two kinds of concave-convex shapes, that is the teacher's face."

This five-character poem clearly portrayed him and was making fun of him, so no wonder he was filled with anger and burst into cursing. After cursing a few times, he immediately turned his face to pay attention to everyone's attitude, wanting to find out who was playing tricks. Little Li, who was known throughout the school for causing trouble, was laughing so hard that he bent over backwards and couldn't be happier. Mr. X believed that it must be his mischief again and reprimanded him sternly. But this trouble was not caused by him, so of course he was unwilling to endure it and stood up to resist, saying

"Mr. X, don't scold people indiscriminately. There is another note posted over there. Please check whether the handwriting is the same and whether it is my handwriting." As he spoke, he pointed to the wall with his hand. Mr. X looked in the direction he pointed and saw a piece of paper posted there. He tore it off and looked at it, knowing that it was another playful poem mocking himself, saying: "The teacher after all loves to be modern, the Western suit on his body is brand new, the most pleasing to the eye is the sculpture of hundreds of flowers on his face."

At this time, he was really so angry that he lost his mind, forgetting to investigate the matter. He didn't even have the mood to teach and picked up his book and ran out of the classroom before the bell rang. From tomorrow onwards, he will sever ties with the school.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Behind the Scenes

Teaching Him a Lesson 219

— Yongnian

That's right, this incident really taught him a lesson, making him understand the dark side of society and making him realize that everything in the past was wrong.

Originally, he was a modern young man, dressed in a Western suit, handsome, and good at social conversation. Therefore, he was very attractive to the opposite sex.

The day before yesterday was Sunday. The X Theater was performing the sensational X Drama. As usual, he dressed up beautifully and went to the X Theater. After entering, his first goal was naturally to find the opposite sex. His sharp rat eyes darted around restlessly, searching for the opposite sex that he wanted in his mind. Upstairs, he suddenly found a member of the opposite sex that he wanted. The clothes of this member of the opposite sex were exceptionally beautiful, and her face and figure were also very modern. Coincidentally, there was an empty seat next to her. He was overjoyed upon seeing this and unceremoniously sat down next to her.

The play was performed, and he watched the stage very calmly. However, his mind was busy figuring out how to start a conversation with her.

After about half an hour, he mustered his courage and said, "Miss... are you... here... alone..." After he said this, his heart was beating very fast.

"..." She didn't say anything, but her body moved slightly and she smiled slightly at him.

He was extremely happy. He knew that she was also interested in him, so he boldly bumped her left arm with his right arm and said again, "Miss... how beautiful."

After repeated temptations, she had been seduced by him. The two of them were slowly getting into a conversation. No one sitting next to them could guess what they were like.

He casually inquired about her background. She told him everything. He then realized that she was the daughter of a wealthy gentleman. He secretly praised his good fortune.

After a while, an usher led a person to them. They were both startled. She took a look and saw that it was her family's maid. She couldn't help asking, "What are you doing here?"

"Miss, I've been looking for you so hard. The master has something urgent to ask you to come back immediately," the maid said breathlessly.

"Ugh... how annoying," she said unhappily. "Let's meet tomorrow, goodbye," she said to him again, "Don't forget, I'll still be waiting for you here tomorrow." She nodded, led the maid, and left gracefully.

After she left, he felt bored, so he also left. When he returned home, he sat down and thought about what had happened. He couldn't help regretting not asking her where she lived, so he could write to her if she didn't come! Suddenly, when he reached into his pocket, his face immediately turned pale. At the same time, he was anxious and flustered. It turned out that his wallet, which contained three hundred yuan in banknotes, was missing. He didn't know when he had lost it. He tried hard to think, but he couldn't remember. In an instant, he suddenly thought of her. It seemed like when he was talking to her, her hand had bumped his pocket. Perhaps she had stolen the wallet. The more he thought about it, the more it seemed likely, and he couldn't help hating her. From then on, when he saw women, he was always hateful and dared not look at them.

Problem

Ah San 220

— 𢛓

The train from N Station had just arrived at S Station, and passengers were scrambling to get off. At that time, people outside the station were soliciting for hotel business, shouting, "Huizhong, Shenzhou, Dongya." Rickshaw drivers were shouting, "Yellow car, Feilong." There were also rickshaw pullers, carriage drivers, and small cart drivers shouting, "Rickshaw, carriage, small cart." The situation at that time was truly chaotic. Rickshaw puller Ah San had not found any business for a day. He waited at the entrance of S Station, hoping to find a customer with good luck.

"Hey, sir, do you need a rickshaw?" Ah San saw a young man in a Western suit standing still, so he hurried to pull his rickshaw next to the young man and asked.

"How much to Lihua Company?" the young man in the Western suit asked.

"Three jiao yuan, is that okay, sir?" Ah San opened his eyes wide and waited for the young man's reply. "Three hundred qian, not a single qian more," the young man in the Western suit replied firmly.

At that time, more and more passengers were gathering, and the noise of cars, carriages, and rickshaw pullers made it difficult for passengers to walk. The police managing security at the station hurriedly hit Ah San with the whip in his hand, driving him away. Ah San was afraid that his license would be torn up by the police, so he hurriedly pulled the rickshaw away as if flying. In an instant, the young man in the Western suit was also gone. Ah San had no choice but to stand there in disappointment, staring blankly at the cars and carriages.

Family Problems

Fuse 221

— Shiben

Master He is truly blessed. He is not yet fifty years old, but he already has two sons, two grandsons, and more than fifty thousand yuan of inherited family property. In our village, he is the most prosperous and fortunate person.

He spends his days smoking opium and playing mahjong, entrusting all family affairs to his eldest son. He does not care about anything himself, which is so leisurely and happy. Moreover, the old couple's love is still very strong, even though they are not young. In addition, his sons and daughters-in-law are very filial to him. Therefore, the entire He family is filled with an atmosphere of harmony and happiness every day. There has never been a disagreement or quarrel. People see his family getting along so well and envy them, saying that the He family is just beginning to prosper.

Stillness leads to restlessness, and satiety leads to lust. These two sentences were unfortunately born in Master He's heart. This spring, Master He was bored at home and went to Shanghai to play. In a hotel, he met a modern woman and was completely charmed by her. Master He regretted not meeting her sooner and spent thousands of yuan to bring her back.

Since this concubine entered the He family's door, the harmonious atmosphere was suddenly broken. Because she is a modern woman, accustomed to a luxurious life in Shanghai, she eats and wears expensive things. How can frugal people like Mrs. He tolerate this extravagant behavior? Therefore, less than a month after she came in, Mrs. He had already started quarreling with her. Originally, Mrs. He was not only stingy with her spending, but the jealousy of vinegar also occupied an important component. But she is not easy to deal with, used to being reckless and domineering, so she would not show weakness. Therefore, when Mrs. He quarreled with her later, she would definitely put on an all-out performance. As a result, Mrs. He was old and had bound feet, how could she be a match for that thick-footed modern madam? She lost and ran to tell her son with a crying face. Originally, Master He's son had long disapproved of bringing this flamboyant young concubine in. He secretly complained that his father should not have brought this troublemaker to squander the family property when he was already old and had children and grandchildren. He thought to himself that this would definitely lead to an uncontrollable situation. Although he complained in his heart, he always remained silent. Now seeing his mother being beaten and insulted by her, he could no longer remain silent. He hurried to reason with her, but in the end, he only had a verbal battle. From then on, Mrs. He resented her husband for doing such an ungrateful act, and she put her former feelings behind her. Every day, she either fought with her or quarreled with her husband. The two sons also disliked the old man for being indecent, bringing this spendthrift to squander the family property, and they became estranged from their father. They were careful in everything and sometimes helped their mother, also arguing with their father and her. All the actions in the family were divided and ruled, each occupying one side and not being subordinate to each other.

Alas! A harmonious family, once a fuse comes, it shatters the entire beautiful state. Husband and wife are not in harmony, father and son are not in harmony. Master He's family, from then on, like our country, often shows a kind of mutually suspicious hostile behavior.

Civil Judgment: Rong Ruichang and others v. Youbang Bank regarding appeal case for debt repayment. The original judgment concerning the appellants jointly repaying the appellee the amount of silver 1,283 taels, 7 mace, and 2 fen is changed. The appellee's request for provisional execution is rejected. The second instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellants. Zheng Axing, namely Zheng Zhitang, v. Gong Shengxiang regarding contract dispute. The appeal of the appellant is rejected. The second instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant. Ji Zhongren and others v. Yitongxing and others regarding mortgage dispute. The appeal of the appellant is rejected. The second instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant. Li Lirenqing v. He Jinlin regarding deposit dispute. The appeal of the appellant is rejected. The second instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant. Xia Yu v. Suolaishi regarding remittance dispute. The principle of the judgment is changed. The appellee's lawsuit is rejected. The first and second instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellee. Maler v. Baoer regarding request for vacating the house, payment of rent arrears, and return of items. The original judgment ordering the appellant to hand over the items listed in the list opened by the appellee one by one is changed. The appellee's lawsuit and incidental appeal regarding the above-mentioned part and the request for provisional execution, and the appellant's remaining appeals are all rejected. One-third of the second instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellee, and the rest shall be borne by the appellant.

Public Service Announcement of Judgment: Lu Kangdi v. Lu Dongsheng and others re: family status dispute appeal. The appeal is rejected. The second instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant.

Criminal Ruling: Xu Zhao氏 for husband Xu Wende committing injury. Upon the petitioner paying a bail of 200 yuan or providing a shop guarantee of 200 yuan, the detention of the defendant Xu Wende shall be suspended.

Criminal Judgment: Shen Yitai re: knowingly purchasing stolen goods appeal. The original judgment is revoked and sent back to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court for retrial. Xu Fengshi v. Xu Zhuting re: defendant's intimidation appeal. The appeal is rejected. Chen Laotaipo, namely Chen Tieshi, re: assisting in abduction appeal. The original judgment is revoked. Shen Baoxing re: endangering the Republic of China appeal. Shen Baoxing prepared to subvert the government by illegal means. He shall be sentenced to one year of imprisonment with a fixed term. The number of days detained before the judgment is determined shall be offset by one day of imprisonment for every two days (above, July 14).

Notice

This court, in the case of creditor Xu Zhoushi suing debtor Gu Xiangsheng over a loan dispute, has already sealed and appraised the debtor Gu Xiangsheng's real estate described below, with the lowest acceptable price recorded. It is now determined that bidding will take place at the court entrance on July 13th, at bidding box number 7. The opening of the bids will take place on July 27th. All residents wishing to purchase the aforementioned real estate are to submit a sealed letter containing their name, age, place of origin, address, occupation, and the amount they are willing to pay. The bid will be opened according to the law on the due date, and the bidder with the highest price will be declared the winner.
